When this IPC handle stammt from a non-pooled source (i.e., a direct tensor without a pool handle), the handle points to a device pointer that was shared via CUDA IPC but the sender might have freed the device buffer after sending.\n\nThe issue is the \"stale device pointer\" - when a tensor from the sender is shared via IPC, the sender keeps the tensor alive (holding a reference), but the sender's tensor may get garbage-collected before the receiver reconstructs it. Under high concurrency, more tensors concurrent and more likely for a sender's tensor to be freed.\n\nLooking at the code flow:\n1. `CudaIpcTensorTransportProxy` is created with a data tensor\n2. `get_proxy_state()` on line 348 extracts the IPC handle from `data.untyped_storage()._share_cuda_()`\n3. In the sglang architecture, there are several processes:\n1. The scheduler process (main process)\n2. The tokenizer process\n3. The tensor parallel worker processes (one per tp rank)\n4. The HTTP worker process\n\nThe CUDA IPC transport is used to share multimodal features between these processes. When the HTTP worker or tokenizer processes sends multimodal data to the scheduler/TP workers, it uses CUDA IPC handles.\n\nLet me read how this works by looking at the infrastructure for ipc transport.\n\nActually, let me focus on what the fix needs to be. The hint says: \"The relevant setting is a sglang environment variable that changes how opened IPC handles are managed **across reuse**.\"\n\nLooking at the environment variables:\n- `SGLANG_USE_CUDA_IPC_TRANSPORT` - Must stay ON (can't disable)\n- `SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE` - Currently False, this changes how opened IPC handles are managed **across reuse**\n- `SGLANG_MM_FEATURE_CACHE_MB` - Scaling the pool\n\nThe key setting is `SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE`. When this is True:\n1. `_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE = True`\n2. `_wrap_tensor_for_cuda_ipc` passes `pool_ipc_handle=self.cudaipc_mmfeature_pool._pool_ipc_handle` to the proxy\n3. On the receiver side, the pooled path is used: `_reconstruct_from_ipc_extra`\n4. The cached handle is opened and cached, keeping a persistent reference to the storage\n\nWhen this is False (the default):\n1. `_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE = False`\n2. `pool_ipc_handle=None` is passed\n3. On the receiver side, the non-pooled path is used: direct `_new_shared_cuda(*redirected_handle)`\n4. No caching is used, and no persistent reference is maintained\n\nThe bug is that without pooling/caching, the IPC handle might become stale. With pooling/caching, the handle is persistently opened and reused, preventing the \"invalid device pointer\" error.\n\nSo the fix is to set `SGLANG_USE_IPC_POOL_HANDLE_CACHE=1` (True).\n\nLet me verify that this is indeed the issue by looking at the log for evidence:\n\n1. Consider increasing SGLANG_MM_FEATURE_CACHE_MB.\"\n\nThis warning appears when the pool runs out of space and falls back to non-IPC. The pool was allocated at 1024MB (1 * 1024 = 1024 MiB). Under high concurrency with many large image features, the pool can fragment and fail to find a large enough chunk.\n\n2.
